			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Effects of global warming</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div role="note" class="hatnote">This article is primarily about effects during the 21st century. For longer-term effects, see <a href="/wiki/Long-term_effects_of_global_warming" title="Long-term effects of global warming">Long-term effects of global warming</a>. See also <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming_on_humans" title="Effects of global warming on humans">Effects of global warming on humans</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Impacts_of_global_warming_2.png" class="image"><img alt="Refer to caption and image description" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Impacts_of_global_warming_2.png/400px-Impacts_of_global_warming_2.png" width="400" height="423" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Impacts_of_global_warming_2.png/600px-Impacts_of_global_warming_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Impacts_of_global_warming_2.png/800px-Impacts_of_global_warming_2.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1268" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Impacts_of_global_warming_2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Summary of climate change impacts.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png" class="image"><img alt="Refer to caption and image description" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png/400px-Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png" width="400" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png/600px-Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png/800px-Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Projected_global_warming_in_2100_for_a_range_of_emission_scenarios.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Projected global warming in 2100 for a range of emission scenarios.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b>effects of <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a></b> are the environmental and social changes caused (directly or indirectly) by human emissions of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a>. There is <a href="/wiki/Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change" title="Scientific opinion on climate change">a scientific consensus that climate change is occurring</a>, and that human activities are the primary driver.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Many impacts of climate change have already been observed, including <a href="/wiki/Retreat_of_glaciers_since_1850" title="Retreat of glaciers since 1850">glacier retreat</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cramer_observed_effects_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cramer_observed_effects-2">[2]</a></sup> changes in the timing of seasonal events<sup id="cite_ref-cramer_observed_effects_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cramer_observed_effects-2">[2]</a></sup> (e.g., earlier flowering of plants),<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> and changes in agricultural productivity.<sup id="cite_ref-cramer_observed_effects_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cramer_observed_effects-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>Future effects of climate change will vary depending on <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_global_warming" title="Politics of global warming">climate change policies</a><sup id="cite_ref-adaptation_and_mitigation_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adaptation_and_mitigation-4">[4]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Social_development" class="mw-redirect" title="Social development">social development</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The two main policies to address climate change are reducing human greenhouse gas emissions (<a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">climate change mitigation</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_adaptation" title="Climate change adaptation">adapting to the impacts</a> of climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-climate_change_policy_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate_change_policy-6">[6]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Climate_engineering" title="Climate engineering">Geoengineering</a> is another policy option.<sup id="cite_ref-climate_change_policy_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-climate_change_policy-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Near-term climate change policies could significantly affect long-term climate change impacts.<sup id="cite_ref-adaptation_and_mitigation_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adaptation_and_mitigation-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Stringent mitigation policies might be able to limit global warming (in 2100) to around 2&#160;<a href="/wiki/%C2%B0C" class="mw-redirect" title="°C">°C</a> or below, relative to pre-industrial levels.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Without mitigation, increased <a href="/wiki/Energy_demand" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy demand">energy demand</a> and extensive use of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> might lead to global warming of around 4&#160;°C.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Higher magnitudes of global warming would be more difficult to adapt to,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and would increase the risk of negative impacts.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definitions">Definitions</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Attribution_of_recent_climate_change" title="Attribution of recent climate change">attribution of recent climate change</a></div>
<p>In this article, "<a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>" means a change in climate that persists over a sustained period of time.<sup id="cite_ref-ipcc_definition_of_climate_change_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc_definition_of_climate_change-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> defines this time period as 30 years.<sup id="cite_ref-ipcc_definition_of_climate_change_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc_definition_of_climate_change-14">[14]</a></sup> Examples of climate change include increases in global surface temperature (global warming), changes in <a href="/wiki/Rainfall" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainfall">rainfall</a> patterns, and changes in the frequency of <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather</a> events. Changes in climate may be due to natural causes, e.g., changes in the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">sun</a>'s output, or due to human activities, e.g., changing the composition of the atmosphere.<sup id="cite_ref-albritton_climate_change_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-albritton_climate_change-16">[16]</a></sup> Any human-induced changes in climate will occur against a background of natural climatic variations<sup id="cite_ref-albritton_climate_change_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-albritton_climate_change-16">[16]</a></sup> and of variations in human activity such as population growth on shores or in arid areas which increase or decrease climate vulnerability.<sup id="cite_ref-NatureTaboo_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NatureTaboo-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also, the term "anthropogenic forcing" refers to the influence exerted on a habitat or chemical environment by humans, as opposed to a natural process.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Temperature_changes">Temperature changes</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:304px;max-width:304px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg" class="image"><img alt="Global mean surface temperature change since 1880, relative to the 1951–1980 mean, showing a long term warming trend." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg/300px-Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg.png" width="300" height="254" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg/450px-Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg/600px-Global_Temperature_Anomaly.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="951" data-file-height="805" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Global mean surface temperature change since 1880, relative to the 1951–1980 mean. Source: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://data.giss.nasa.gov/gistemp/">NASA GISS</a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_(2007).png" class="image"><img alt="Refer to caption" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.png/300px-Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.png" width="300" height="139" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.png/450px-Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.png/600px-Projected_global_warming_over_the_21st_century_using_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.png 2x" data-file-width="728" data-file-height="338" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The graph above shows the average of a set of temperature simulations for the 20th century (black line), followed by projected temperatures for the 21st century based on three greenhouse gas emissions scenarios (colored lines).<sup id="cite_ref-herring_temperature_projections_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-herring_temperature_projections-19">[19]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This article breaks down some of the impacts of climate change according to different levels of future global warming. This way of describing impacts has, for instance, been used in the IPCC (<a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a>) Assessment Reports on climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-table_of_key_vulnerabilities_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-table_of_key_vulnerabilities-20">[20]</a></sup> The instrumental <a href="/wiki/Temperature_record" title="Temperature record">temperature record</a> shows global warming of around 0.6&#160;°C during the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Observed_changes_in_climate_and_their_effects_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Observed_changes_in_climate_and_their_effects-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="SRES_emissions_scenarios">SRES emissions scenarios</span></h3>
<p>The future level of global warming is uncertain, but a wide range of estimates (projections) have been made.<sup id="cite_ref-Overview_of_GHG_emissions_scenarios_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overview_of_GHG_emissions_scenarios-22">[22]</a></sup> The IPCC's "<a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">SRES</a>" scenarios have been frequently used to make <a href="/wiki/Global_climate_model#Projections_of_future_climate_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Global climate model">projections of future climate change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USGCRP_exec_sum_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGCRP_exec_sum-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:22–24</sup> The SRES scenarios are "<a href="/wiki/Economics_of_climate_change_mitigation#Baselines" title="Economics of climate change mitigation">baseline</a>" (or "reference") scenarios, which means that they do not take into account any current or future measures to limit GHG emissions (e.g., the UNFCCC's <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference" title="2010 United Nations Climate Change Conference">Cancún agreements</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Emissions projections of the SRES scenarios are broadly comparable in range to the baseline emissions scenarios that have been developed by the scientific community.<sup id="cite_ref-Overview_of_GHG_emissions_scenarios_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overview_of_GHG_emissions_scenarios-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Fourth_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Fourth Assessment Report">IPCC Fourth Assessment Report</a>, changes in future global mean temperature were projected using the six SRES "marker" emissions scenarios.<sup id="cite_ref-Table_of_global_warming_projections_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Table_of_global_warming_projections-26">[26]</a></sup> Emissions projections for the six SRES "marker" scenarios are representative of the full set of forty SRES scenarios.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> For the lowest emissions SRES marker scenario ("B1" - see the <a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">SRES</a> article for details on this scenario), the best estimate for global mean temperature is an increase of 1.8&#160;°C (3.2&#160;°F)<sup id="cite_ref-Table_of_global_warming_projections_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Table_of_global_warming_projections-26">[26]</a></sup> by the end of the 21st century. This projection is relative to global temperatures at the end of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The "likely" range (greater than 66% probability, based on expert judgement)<sup id="cite_ref-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty-29">[29]</a></sup> for the SRES B1 marker scenario is 1.1–2.9&#160;°C (2.0–5.2&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Table_of_global_warming_projections_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Table_of_global_warming_projections-26">[26]</a></sup> For the highest emissions SRES marker scenario (A1FI), the best estimate for global mean temperature increase is 4.0&#160;°C (7.2&#160;°F), with a "likely" range of 2.4–6.4&#160;°C (4.3–11.5&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-Table_of_global_warming_projections_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Table_of_global_warming_projections-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The range in temperature projections partly reflects (1) the choice of <a href="/wiki/Economics_of_global_warming#Emissions_scenarios" title="Economics of global warming">emissions scenario</a>, and (2) the "<a href="/wiki/Climate_sensitivity" title="Climate sensitivity">climate sensitivity</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-USGCRP_exec_sum_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGCRP_exec_sum-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:22–24</sup> For (1), different scenarios make different assumptions of future social and economic development (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">economic growth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Population_projection" title="Population projection">population level</a>, <a href="/wiki/Energy_policy" title="Energy policy">energy policies</a>), which in turn affects projections of greenhouse gas (GHG) emissions.<sup id="cite_ref-USGCRP_exec_sum_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGCRP_exec_sum-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:22–24</sup> The projected magnitude of warming by 2100 is closely related to the level of cumulative emissions over the 21st century (i.e. total emissions between 2000-2100).<sup id="cite_ref-unep_cumulative_emissions_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unep_cumulative_emissions-30">[30]</a></sup> The higher the cumulative emissions over this time period, the greater the level of warming is projected to occur.<sup id="cite_ref-unep_cumulative_emissions_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unep_cumulative_emissions-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>(2) reflects uncertainty in the response of the climate system to past and future GHG emissions, which is measured by the <a href="/wiki/Climate_sensitivity" title="Climate sensitivity">climate sensitivity</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-USGCRP_exec_sum_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGCRP_exec_sum-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:22–24</sup> Higher estimates of climate sensitivity lead to greater projected warming, while lower estimates of climate sensitivity lead to less projected warming.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over the next several millennia, projections suggest that global warming could be irreversible.<sup id="cite_ref-solomon_irreversible_climate_change_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_irreversible_climate_change-32">[32]</a></sup> Even if emissions were drastically reduced, global temperatures would remain close to their highest level for at least 1,000 years (see the later section on <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming#Irreversibilities" title="Effects of global warming">irreversibilities</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>

</div>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Scientists have used various "proxy" data to assess past changes in Earth's climate (<a href="/wiki/Paleoclimate" class="mw-redirect" title="Paleoclimate">paleoclimate</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-noaa_proxy_climate_data_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-noaa_proxy_climate_data-36">[36]</a></sup> Sources of proxy data include historical records (such as <a href="/wiki/Farmer" title="Farmer">farmers</a>' logs), <a href="/wiki/Tree_ring" class="mw-redirect" title="Tree ring">tree rings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">corals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fossil_pollen" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil pollen">fossil pollen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_core" title="Ice core">ice cores</a>, and ocean and lake <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">sediments</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-noaa_proxy_climate_data_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-noaa_proxy_climate_data-36">[36]</a></sup> Analysis of these data suggest that recent warming is unusual in the past 400 years, possibly longer.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> By the end of the 21st century, temperatures may increase to a level not experienced since the mid-<a href="/wiki/Pliocene" title="Pliocene">Pliocene</a>, around 3 million years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-jansen_pliocene_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jansen_pliocene-38">[38]</a></sup> At that time, models suggest that mean global temperatures were about 2–3&#160;°C warmer than pre-industrial temperatures.<sup id="cite_ref-jansen_pliocene_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jansen_pliocene-38">[38]</a></sup> Even a 2&#160;°C rise above the pre-industrial level would be outside the range of temperatures experienced by human <a href="/wiki/Civilization" title="Civilization">civilization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hansen_climate_history_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hansen_climate_history-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_impacts">Physical impacts</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Physical_impacts_of_climate_change" title="Physical impacts of climate change">Physical impacts of climate change</a></div>
<table>
<tr>
<td>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png" class="image"><img alt="Refer to caption and adjacent text" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png/450px-Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png" width="450" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png/675px-Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png/900px-Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png 2x" data-file-width="3191" data-file-height="1691" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Diagram_showing_ten_indicators_of_global_warming.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Seven of these indicators would be expected to increase in a warming world and observations show that they are, in fact, increasing. Three would be expected to decrease and they are, in fact, decreasing.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png" class="image"><img alt="Refer to caption" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png/350px-Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png" width="350" height="540" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png/525px-Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png/700px-Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="3242" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Changes_in_climate_indicators_that_show_global_warming.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
This set of graphs show changes in climate indicators over several decades. Each of the different colored lines in each panel represents an independently analyzed set of data. The data come from many different technologies including <a href="/wiki/Weather_station" title="Weather station">weather stations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weather_balloons" class="mw-redirect" title="Weather balloons">weather balloons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ship" title="Ship">ships</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buoy" title="Buoy">buoys</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A broad range of evidence shows that the climate system has warmed.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Evidence of global warming is shown in the graphs opposite. Some of the graphs show a positive <a href="/wiki/Trend_estimation" class="mw-redirect" title="Trend estimation">trend</a>, e.g., increasing temperature over land and the ocean, and <a href="/wiki/Current_sea_level_rise" class="mw-redirect" title="Current sea level rise">sea level rise</a>. Other graphs show a negative trend, e.g., decreased <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">snow</a> cover in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a>, and declining <a href="/wiki/Arctic_sea_ice" class="mw-redirect" title="Arctic sea ice">Arctic sea ice</a> extent. Evidence of warming is also apparent in living <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming#Observed_impacts_on_biological_systems" title="Effects of global warming">(biological) systems</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rosenzweig_observed_impacts_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rosenzweig_observed_impacts-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Human activities have contributed to a number of the observed changes in climate.<sup id="cite_ref-hegerl_climate_change_attribution_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hegerl_climate_change_attribution-44">[44]</a></sup> This contribution has principally been through the burning of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a>, which has led to an increase in the concentration of GHGs in the atmosphere.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Another human influence on the climate are <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a> emissions, which are a precursor to the formation of <a href="/wiki/Sulfate_aerosols" class="mw-redirect" title="Sulfate aerosols">sulfate aerosols</a> in the atmosphere.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>Human-induced warming could lead to <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming#Abrupt_or_irreversible_changes" title="Effects of global warming">large-scale, irreversible, and/or abrupt changes</a> in physical systems.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> An example of this is the melting of <a href="/wiki/Ice_sheet" title="Ice sheet">ice sheets</a>, which contributes to sea level rise.<sup id="cite_ref-magnitudes_of_impact_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-magnitudes_of_impact-49">[49]</a></sup> The probability of warming having unforeseen consequences increases with the rate, magnitude, and duration of climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_weather">Effects on weather</span></h3>
<p>Observations show that there have been changes in weather.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> As climate changes, the <a href="/wiki/Probabilities" class="mw-redirect" title="Probabilities">probabilities</a> of certain types of weather events are affected.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century,_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario,_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png" class="image"><img alt="refer to caption and adjacent text" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century%2C_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario%2C_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png/250px-Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century%2C_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario%2C_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png" width="250" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century%2C_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario%2C_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png/375px-Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century%2C_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario%2C_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century%2C_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario%2C_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png/500px-Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century%2C_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario%2C_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Projected_change_in_annual_average_precipitation_for_the_21st_century,_based_on_the_SRES_A1B_emissions_scenario,_and_simulated_by_the_GFDL_CM2.1_model.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Projected change in annual average precipitation by the end of the 21st century, based on a medium emissions scenario (<a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">SRES</a> A1B) (Credit: NOAA <a href="/wiki/Geophysical_Fluid_Dynamics_Laboratory" title="Geophysical Fluid Dynamics Laboratory">Geophysical Fluid Dynamics Laboratory</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gfdl_rainfall_projections_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gfdl_rainfall_projections-53">[53]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Changes have been observed in the amount, intensity, frequency, and type of <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-USGCRP_exec_sum_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGCRP_exec_sum-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:18</sup> Widespread increases in heavy precipitation have occurred, even in places where total rain amounts have decreased. With medium confidence (see <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming#Footnotes" title="Effects of global warming">footnote 1</a>), IPCC (2012)<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> concluded that human influences had contributed to an increase in heavy precipitation events at the global scale.</p>
<p>Projections of future changes in precipitation show overall increases in the global average, but with substantial shifts in where and how precipitation falls.<sup id="cite_ref-USGCRP_exec_sum_23-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGCRP_exec_sum-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:24</sup> Projections suggest a reduction in rainfall in the <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">subtropics</a>, and an increase in precipitation in subpolar latitudes and some <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Equatorial region">equatorial regions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gfdl_rainfall_projections_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gfdl_rainfall_projections-53">[53]</a></sup> In other words, regions which are dry at present will in general become even drier, while regions that are currently wet will in general become even wetter.<sup id="cite_ref-gfdl_rainfall_projections_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gfdl_rainfall_projections-53">[53]</a></sup> This projection does not apply to every locale, and in some cases can be modified by local conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-gfdl_rainfall_projections_53-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gfdl_rainfall_projections-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Extreme_weather">Extreme weather</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">Extreme weather</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone#Global_warming" title="Tropical cyclone">Tropical cyclone §&#160;Global warming</a></div>
<p>Over most land areas since the 1950s, it is very likely that there have been fewer or warmer cold days and nights.<sup id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">[55]</a></sup> Hot days and nights have also very likely become warmer or more frequent.<sup id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">[55]</a></sup> Human activities have very likely contributed to these trends.<sup id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">[55]</a></sup> There may have been changes in other climate extremes (e.g., <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">floods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">droughts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclones</a>) but these changes are more difficult to identify.<sup id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Projections suggest changes in the frequency and intensity of some extreme weather events.<sup id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">[55]</a></sup> Confidence in projections varies over time.<sup id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Near-term projections (2016–2035)</dt>
</dl>
<p>Some changes (e.g., more frequent hot days) will probably be evident in the near term, while other near-term changes (e.g., more intense droughts and tropical cyclones) are more uncertain.<sup id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Long-term projections (2081–2100)</dt>
</dl>
<p>Future climate change will be associated with more very hot days and fewer very cold days.<sup id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">[55]</a></sup> The frequency, length and intensity of <a href="/wiki/Heat_wave" title="Heat wave">heat waves</a> will very likely increase over most land areas.<sup id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">[55]</a></sup> Higher growth in anthropogenic GHG emissions will be associated with larger increases in the frequency and severity of temperature extremes.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>Assuming high growth in GHG emissions (IPCC scenario <a href="/wiki/Representative_Concentration_Pathways" title="Representative Concentration Pathways">RCP8.5</a>), presently dry regions may be affected by an increase in the risk of drought and reductions in <a href="/wiki/Soil_moisture" class="mw-redirect" title="Soil moisture">soil moisture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Over most of the mid-latitude land masses and wet tropical regions, extreme precipitation events will very likely become more intense and frequent.<sup id="cite_ref-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes_55-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar5_wg1_climate_extremes-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Tropical cyclones</dt>
</dl>
<p>At the global scale, the frequency of tropical cyclones will probably decrease or be unchanged.<sup id="cite_ref-christensen_2013_cyclones_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-christensen_2013_cyclones-58">[58]</a></sup> Global mean tropical cyclone maximum wind speed and precipitation rates will likely increase.<sup id="cite_ref-christensen_2013_cyclones_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-christensen_2013_cyclones-58">[58]</a></sup> Changes in tropical cyclones will probably vary by region, but these variations are uncertain.<sup id="cite_ref-christensen_2013_cyclones_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-christensen_2013_cyclones-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>Effects of climate extremes</dt>
</dl>
<p>The impacts of extreme events on the environment and human society will vary. Some impacts will be beneficial—e.g., fewer cold extremes will probably lead to fewer cold deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-health_summary_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-health_summary-59">[59]</a></sup> Overall, however, impacts will probably be mostly negative.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ar4_synthesis_reasons_for_concern_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_synthesis_reasons_for_concern-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cryosphere">Cryosphere</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Retreat_of_glaciers_since_1850" title="Retreat of glaciers since 1850">Retreat of glaciers since 1850</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="refer to caption and adjacent text" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png/220px-Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png/330px-Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png/440px-Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="477" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Glacier_Mass_Balance_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A map of the change in thickness of mountain glaciers since 1970. Thinning in orange and red, thickening in blue.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="2012 Arctic sea ice extent" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/97/SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg/220px-SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/97/SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg/330px-SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/97/SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg/440px-SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="770" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SeaIce-Sept162012_HR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A map that shows ice concentration on 16 September 2012, along with the extent of the previous record low (yellow line) and the mid-September median extent (black line) setting a new record low that was 18 percent smaller than the previous record and nearly 50 percent smaller than the long-term (1979-2000) average.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cryosphere" title="Cryosphere">cryosphere</a> is made up of areas of the Earth which are covered by snow or ice.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Observed changes in the cryosphere include declines in <a href="/wiki/Arctic_sea_ice" class="mw-redirect" title="Arctic sea ice">Arctic sea ice</a> extent,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> the widespread retreat of <a href="/wiki/Alpine_glaciers" class="mw-redirect" title="Alpine glaciers">alpine glaciers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> and reduced snow cover in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>Solomon <i>et al.</i> (2007)<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_arctic_sea_ice_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_arctic_sea_ice-66">[66]</a></sup> assessed the potential impacts of climate change on <a href="/wiki/Summer" title="Summer">summertime</a> Arctic sea ice extent. Assuming high growth in greenhouse gas emissions (<a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">SRES A2</a>), some models projected that Arctic sea ice in the summer could largely disappear by the end of the 21st century.<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_arctic_sea_ice_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_arctic_sea_ice-66">[66]</a></sup> More recent projections suggest that the Arctic summers could be ice-free (defined as ice extent less than 1 million square km) as early as 2025-2030.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 21st century, glaciers<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> and snow cover are projected to continue their widespread retreat.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In the western mountains of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, increasing temperatures and changes in precipitation are projected to lead to reduced <a href="/wiki/Snowpack" title="Snowpack">snowpack</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Snowpack is the seasonal accumulation of slow-melting snow.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The melting of the <a href="/wiki/Greenland_ice_sheet" title="Greenland ice sheet">Greenland</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Antarctic_ice_sheet" class="mw-redirect" title="West Antarctic ice sheet">West Antarctic ice sheets</a> could contribute to sea level rise, especially over long time-scales (see the section on <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming#Greenland_and_West_Antarctic_Ice_sheets" title="Effects of global warming">Greenland and West Antarctic Ice sheets</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-magnitudes_of_impact_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-magnitudes_of_impact-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>Changes in the cryosphere are projected to have social impacts.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> For example, in some regions, glacier retreat could increase the risk of reductions in seasonal water availability.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Barnett <i>et al.</i> (2005)<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> estimated that more than one-sixth of the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_population" class="mw-redirect" title="World's population">world's population</a> rely on glaciers and snowpack for their water supply.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceans">Oceans</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming_on_oceans" title="Effects of global warming on oceans">Effects of global warming on oceans</a></div>
<p>The role of the oceans in global warming is complex. The oceans serve as a sink for carbon dioxide, taking up much that would otherwise remain in the atmosphere, but increased levels of <span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
2</span></span> have led to <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">ocean acidification</a>. Furthermore, as the temperature of the oceans increases, they become less able to absorb excess <span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
2</span></span>. The ocean have also acted as a sink in absorbing extra heat from the atmosphere.<sup id="cite_ref-statecl_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statecl-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:4</sup> The increase in ocean <a href="/wiki/Heat_content" class="mw-redirect" title="Heat content">heat content</a> is much larger than any other store of <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a> in the Earth’s heat balance over the two periods 1961 to 2003 and 1993 to 2003, and accounts for more than 90% of the possible increase in heat content of the Earth system during these periods.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Global warming is projected to have a number of effects on the oceans. Ongoing effects include rising sea levels due to thermal expansion and melting of glaciers and ice sheets, and warming of the ocean surface, leading to increased temperature stratification. Other possible effects include large-scale changes in ocean circulation.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Acidification">Acidification</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ocean_acidification" title="Ocean acidification">Ocean acidification</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans,_1880-2012_(US_EPA).png" class="image"><img alt="refer to caption and image description" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans%2C_1880-2012_%28US_EPA%29.png/220px-Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans%2C_1880-2012_%28US_EPA%29.png" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans%2C_1880-2012_%28US_EPA%29.png/330px-Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans%2C_1880-2012_%28US_EPA%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans%2C_1880-2012_%28US_EPA%29.png/440px-Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans%2C_1880-2012_%28US_EPA%29.png 2x" data-file-width="670" data-file-height="536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Changes_in_aragonite_saturation_of_the_world%27s_oceans,_1880-2012_(US_EPA).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
This map shows changes in the amount of <a href="/wiki/Aragonite" title="Aragonite">aragonite</a> dissolved in <a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">ocean</a> surface waters between the 1880s and the most recent decade (2003-2012).<sup id="cite_ref-us_epa_2012_aragonite_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us_epa_2012_aragonite-77">[77]</a></sup> Historical modeling suggests that since the 1880s, increased CO<sub>2</sub> has led to lower <a href="/wiki/Aragonite" title="Aragonite">aragonite</a> saturation levels (less availability of minerals) in the oceans around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-us_epa_2012_aragonite_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us_epa_2012_aragonite-77">[77]</a></sup> The largest decreases in aragonite saturation have occurred in <a href="/wiki/Tropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical">tropical</a> waters.<sup id="cite_ref-us_epa_2012_aragonite_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us_epa_2012_aragonite-77">[77]</a></sup> However, decreases in cold areas may be of greater concern because colder waters typically have lower aragonite levels to begin with.<sup id="cite_ref-us_epa_2012_aragonite_77-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us_epa_2012_aragonite-77">[77]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>About one-third of the carbon dioxide emitted by human activity has already been taken up by the oceans.<sup id="cite_ref-nrc_2008b_ocean_acidification_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nrc_2008b_ocean_acidification-78">[78]</a></sup> As carbon dioxide dissolves in <a href="/wiki/Sea_water" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea water">sea water</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carbonic_acid" title="Carbonic acid">carbonic acid</a> is formed, which has the effect of acidifying the ocean, measured as a change in <a href="/wiki/PH" title="PH">pH</a>. The uptake of human carbon emissions since the year 1750 has led to an average decrease in pH of 0.1 units.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_AR4_ocean_acidification_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_AR4_ocean_acidification-79">[79]</a></sup> Projections using the SRES emissions scenarios suggest a further reduction in average global surface ocean pH of between 0.14 and 0.35 units over the 21st century.</p>
<p>The effects of ocean acidification on the marine <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">biosphere</a> have yet to be documented.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_AR4_ocean_acidification_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_AR4_ocean_acidification-79">[79]</a></sup> Laboratory experiments suggest beneficial effects for a few species, with potentially highly detrimental effects for a substantial number of species.<sup id="cite_ref-nrc_2008b_ocean_acidification_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nrc_2008b_ocean_acidification-78">[78]</a></sup> With medium confidence, Fischlin <i>et al.</i> (2007)<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> projected that future ocean acidification and climate change would impair a wide range of <a href="/wiki/Plankton" title="Plankton">planktonic</a> and shallow <a href="/wiki/Benthos" title="Benthos">benthic</a> marine organisms that use <a href="/wiki/Aragonite" title="Aragonite">aragonite</a> to make their shells or skeletons, such as <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">corals</a> and marine <a href="/wiki/Snail" title="Snail">snails</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pteropoda" title="Pteropoda">pteropods</a>), with significant impacts particularly in the Southern Ocean.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Oxygen_depletion">Oxygen depletion</span></h4>
<p>The amount of oxygen dissolved in the oceans may decline, with adverse consequences for ocean life.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sea_level_rise">Sea level rise</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Current_sea_level_rise" class="mw-redirect" title="Current sea level rise">Current sea level rise</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Future_sea_level" title="Future sea level">Future sea level</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level,_1870-2008_(US_EPA).png" class="image"><img alt="refer to caption and adjacent text" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level%2C_1870-2008_%28US_EPA%29.png/220px-Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level%2C_1870-2008_%28US_EPA%29.png" width="220" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level%2C_1870-2008_%28US_EPA%29.png/330px-Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level%2C_1870-2008_%28US_EPA%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level%2C_1870-2008_%28US_EPA%29.png/440px-Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level%2C_1870-2008_%28US_EPA%29.png 2x" data-file-width="670" data-file-height="717" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Trends_in_global_average_absolute_sea_level,_1870-2008_(US_EPA).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Trends in global average absolute sea level, 1870-2008.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There is strong evidence that global sea level rose gradually over the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FAQ_5.1_is_sea_level_rising_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAQ_5.1_is_sea_level_rising-84">[84]</a></sup> With high confidence, Bindoff <i>et al.</i> (2007)<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> concluded that between the mid-19th and mid-20th centuries, the rate of sea level rise increased. Authors of the IPCC Fourth Assessment Synthesis Report (IPCC AR4 SYR, 2007)<sup id="cite_ref-Observed_changes_in_climate_and_their_effects_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Observed_changes_in_climate_and_their_effects-21">[21]</a></sup> reported that between the years 1961 and 2003, global average sea level rose at an average rate of 1.8&#160;mm per year (mm/yr), with a range of 1.3–2.3&#160;mm/yr. Between 1993 and 2003, the rate increased above the previous period to 3.1&#160;mm/yr (range of 2.4–3.8&#160;mm/yr). Authors of IPCC AR4 SYR (2007)<sup id="cite_ref-Observed_changes_in_climate_and_their_effects_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Observed_changes_in_climate_and_their_effects-21">[21]</a></sup> were uncertain whether the increase in rate from 1993 to 2003 was due to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change#Internal_forcing_mechanisms" title="Climate change">natural variations</a> in sea level over the time period, or whether it reflected an increase in the underlying long-term trend.</p>
<p>There are two main factors that have contributed to observed sea level rise.<sup id="cite_ref-FAQ_5.1_is_sea_level_rising_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAQ_5.1_is_sea_level_rising-84">[84]</a></sup> The first is <a href="/wiki/Thermal_expansion" title="Thermal expansion">thermal expansion</a>: as ocean water warms, it expands.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The second is from the contribution of land-based ice due to increased melting. The major store of water on land is found in glaciers and ice sheets. Anthropogenic forces very likely (greater than 90% probability, based on expert judgement)<sup id="cite_ref-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty-29">[29]</a></sup> contributed to sea level rise during the latter half of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-hegerl_climate_change_attribution_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hegerl_climate_change_attribution-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is a widespread consensus that substantial long-term sea level rise will continue for centuries to come.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> In their Fourth Assessment Report, the IPCC<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> projected sea level rise to the end of the 21st century using the SRES emissions scenarios. Across the six SRES marker scenarios, sea level was projected to rise by 18 to 59&#160;cm (7.1 to 23.2&#160;in), relative to sea level at the end of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Thermal expansion is the largest component in these projections, contributing 70-75% of the central estimate for all scenarios.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Due to a lack of scientific understanding, this sea level rise estimate does not include all of the possible contributions of ice sheets (see the section on <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming#Greenland_and_West_Antarctic_Ice_sheets" title="Effects of global warming">Greenland and West Antarctic Ice sheets</a>).</p>
<p>An assessment of the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_literature" title="Scientific literature">scientific literature</a> on climate change was published in 2010 by the <a href="/wiki/US_National_Research_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="US National Research Council">US National Research Council</a> (US NRC, 2010).<sup id="cite_ref-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise-91">[91]</a></sup> NRC (2010)<sup id="cite_ref-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise-91">[91]</a></sup> described the projections in AR4 (i.e. those cited in the above paragraph) as "conservative", and summarized the results of more recent studies. Cited studies suggested a great deal of uncertainty in projections.<sup id="cite_ref-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise-91">[91]</a></sup> A range of projections suggested possible sea level rise by the end of the 21st century of between 0.56 and 2 m, relative to sea levels at the end of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise_91-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRC_2010_projections_of_sea_level_rise-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ocean_temperature_rise">Ocean temperature rise</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heat_content700m2000myr.png" class="image"><img alt="Global ocean heat content" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6f/Heat_content700m2000myr.png/220px-Heat_content700m2000myr.png" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6f/Heat_content700m2000myr.png/330px-Heat_content700m2000myr.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6f/Heat_content700m2000myr.png/440px-Heat_content700m2000myr.png 2x" data-file-width="566" data-file-height="380" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heat_content700m2000myr.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Global ocean heat content from 1955-2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From 1961 to 2003, the global ocean temperature has risen by 0.10&#160;°C from the surface to a depth of 700 m. There is variability both year-to-year and over longer time scales, with global ocean heat content observations showing high rates of warming for 1991–2003, but some cooling from 2003 to 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The temperature of the Antarctic <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">Southern Ocean</a> rose by 0.17&#160;°C (0.31&#160;°F) between the 1950s and the 1980s, nearly twice the rate for the world's oceans as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> As well as having effects on ecosystems (e.g. by melting sea ice, affecting algae that grow on its underside), warming reduces the ocean's ability to absorb <span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><br />
2</span></span>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It is likely (greater than 66% probability, based on expert judgement)<sup id="cite_ref-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc_ar4_uncertainty-29">[29]</a></sup> that anthropogenic forcing contributed to the general warming observed in the upper several hundred metres of the ocean during the latter half of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-hegerl_climate_change_attribution_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hegerl_climate_change_attribution-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Regions">Regions</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Regional_effects_of_global_warming" title="Regional effects of global warming">Regional effects of global warming</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:304px;max-width:304px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Temperatures_across_the_world_in_the_1880s_(left)_and_the_1980s_(right),_as_compared_to_average_temperatures_from_1951_to_1980_(US_EPA).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Temperatures in most parts of the world were warmer in the 1980s compared to the 1880s" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Temperatures_across_the_world_in_the_1880s_%28left%29_and_the_1980s_%28right%29%2C_as_compared_to_average_temperatures_from_1951_to_1980_%28US_EPA%29.jpg/300px-Temperatures_across_the_world_in_the_1880s_%28left%29_and_the_1980s_%28right%29%2C_as_compared_to_average_temperatures_from_1951_to_1980_%28US_EPA%29.jpg" width="300" height="83" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Temperatures_across_the_world_in_the_1880s_%28left%29_and_the_1980s_%28right%29%2C_as_compared_to_average_temperatures_from_1951_to_1980_%28US_EPA%29.jpg/450px-Temperatures_across_the_world_in_the_1880s_%28left%29_and_the_1980s_%28right%29%2C_as_compared_to_average_temperatures_from_1951_to_1980_%28US_EPA%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Temperatures_across_the_world_in_the_1880s_%28left%29_and_the_1980s_%28right%29%2C_as_compared_to_average_temperatures_from_1951_to_1980_%28US_EPA%29.jpg/600px-Temperatures_across_the_world_in_the_1880s_%28left%29_and_the_1980s_%28right%29%2C_as_compared_to_average_temperatures_from_1951_to_1980_%28US_EPA%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="333" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Temperatures across the world in the 1880s (left) and the 1980s (right), as compared to average temperatures from 1951 to 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_(2007).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Future warming across the globe varies according to different projections of greenhouse gas emissions" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.jpg/300px-Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.jpg" width="300" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.jpg/450px-Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.jpg/600px-Map_of_projected_global_warming_across_the_globe_by_the_2050s._Projections_based_on_three_SRES_greenhouse_gas_emissions_scenarios._Data_from_CMIP3_%282007%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="360" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Projected changes in average temperatures across the world in the 2050s under three greenhouse gas (GHG) <a href="/wiki/Economics_of_global_warming#Emissions_scenarios" title="Economics of global warming">emissions scenarios</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-herring_temperature_projections_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-herring_temperature_projections-19">[19]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Regional effects of global warming vary in nature. Some are the result of a generalised global change, such as rising temperature, resulting in local effects, such as melting ice. In other cases, a change may be related to a change in a particular ocean current or weather system. In such cases, the regional effect may be disproportionate and will not necessarily follow the global trend.</p>
<p>There are three major ways in which global warming will make changes to regional climate: melting or forming ice, changing the <a href="/wiki/Hydrological_cycle" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrological cycle">hydrological cycle</a> (of <a href="/wiki/Evaporation" title="Evaporation">evaporation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a>) and changing <a href="/wiki/Ocean_current" title="Ocean current">currents in the oceans</a> and air flows in the atmosphere. The coast can also be considered a region, and will suffer severe impacts from <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">sea level rise</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Observed_impacts">Observed impacts</span></h3>
<p>With very high confidence, Rosenzweig <i>et al.</i> (2007)<sup id="cite_ref-rosenzweig_observed_impacts_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rosenzweig_observed_impacts-43">[43]</a></sup> concluded that physical and biological systems on all continents and in most oceans had been affected by recent climate changes, particularly regional temperature increases. Impacts include earlier leafing of <a href="/wiki/Tree" title="Tree">trees</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">plants</a> over many regions; movements of species to higher latitudes and altitudes in the Northern Hemisphere; changes in <a href="/wiki/Bird_migration" title="Bird migration">bird migrations</a> in Europe, North America and Australia; and shifting of the oceans' <a href="/wiki/Plankton" title="Plankton">plankton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a> from cold- to warm-adapted communities.<sup id="cite_ref-nasa_briefs_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nasa_briefs-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>The human influence on the climate can be seen in the geographical pattern of observed warming, with greater temperature increases over land and in <a href="/wiki/Polar_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Polar region">polar regions</a> rather than over the oceans.<sup id="cite_ref-nrc_2008_climate_change_brochure_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nrc_2008_climate_change_brochure-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:6</sup> Using models, it is possible to identify the human "signal" of global warming over both land and ocean areas.<sup id="cite_ref-nrc_2008_climate_change_brochure_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nrc_2008_climate_change_brochure-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:6</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Projected_impacts">Projected impacts</span></h3>
<p>Projections of future climate changes at the regional scale do not hold as high a level of scientific confidence as projections made at the global scale.<sup id="cite_ref-nrc_2008_climate_change_brochure_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nrc_2008_climate_change_brochure-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:9</sup> It is, however, expected that future warming will follow a similar geographical pattern to that seen already, with greatest warming over land and high northern <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitudes</a>, and least over the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">Southern Ocean</a> and parts of the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_Ocean" class="mw-redirect" title="North Atlantic Ocean">North Atlantic Ocean</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Nearly all land areas will very likely warm more than the global average.<sup id="cite_ref-tar_table_of_robust_findings_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_table_of_robust_findings-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, small islands and <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asian</a> <a href="/wiki/River_delta" title="River delta">megadeltas</a> are regions that are likely to be especially affected by climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_especially_affected_regions_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_especially_affected_regions-99">[99]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">Low-latitude</a>, <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">less-developed</a> areas are at most risk of experiencing negative impacts due to climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-schneider_distribution_of_impacts_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schneider_distribution_of_impacts-100">[100]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Developed_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Developed countries">Developed countries</a> are also vulnerable to climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-schneider_regional_vulnerabilities_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schneider_regional_vulnerabilities-101">[101]</a></sup> For example, developed countries will be negatively affected by increases in the severity and frequency of some <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather</a> events, such as <a href="/wiki/Heat_wave" title="Heat wave">heat waves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-schneider_regional_vulnerabilities_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schneider_regional_vulnerabilities-101">[101]</a></sup> In all regions, some people can be particularly at risk from climate change, such as the <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poor</a>, young <a href="/wiki/Children" class="mw-redirect" title="Children">children</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Elderly" class="mw-redirect" title="Elderly">elderly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_especially_affected_regions_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_especially_affected_regions-99">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-schneider_distribution_of_impacts_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schneider_distribution_of_impacts-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_systems">Social systems</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_climate_change_on_humans" class="mw-redirect" title="Effects of climate change on humans">Effects of climate change on humans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change,_industry_and_society" title="Climate change, industry and society">Climate change, industry and society</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_gender" title="Climate change and gender">Climate change and gender</a></div>
<p>The impacts of climate change can be thought of in terms of sensitivity and vulnerability. "Sensitivity" is the degree to which a particular system or sector might be affected, positively or negatively, by climate change and/or <a href="/wiki/Climate_change#Causes" title="Climate change">climate variability</a>. "Vulnerability" is the degree to which a particular system or sector might be adversely affected by climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>The sensitivity of human society to climate change varies. Sectors sensitive to climate change include water resources, coastal zones, human settlements, and human health. Industries sensitive to climate change include <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_agriculture" title="Climate change and agriculture">agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fisheries_and_climate_change" title="Fisheries and climate change">fisheries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Energy_industry" title="Energy industry">energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Construction" title="Construction">construction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Insurance" title="Insurance">insurance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Recreation" title="Recreation">recreation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_supply">Food supply</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_and_agriculture" title="Climate change and agriculture">Climate change and agriculture</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Food_security" title="Food security">Food security</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_vs_fuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Food vs fuel">Food vs fuel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932008_world_food_price_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2007–2008 world food price crisis">2007–2008 world food price crisis</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png/220px-Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png/330px-Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png/440px-Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png 2x" data-file-width="1448" data-file-height="1074" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Net_crops_tropicalvsworld.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Graph of net crop production worldwide and in selected tropical countries. Raw data from the United Nations. <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://faostat3.fao.org/browse/Q/QC/E">[2]</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Climate change will impact agriculture and food production around the world due to: the effects of elevated CO<sub>2</sub> in the atmosphere, higher temperatures, altered precipitation and <a href="/wiki/Transpiration" title="Transpiration">transpiration</a> regimes, increased frequency of extreme events, and modified <a href="/wiki/Weed" title="Weed">weed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pest_(organism)" title="Pest (organism)">pest</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pathogen" title="Pathogen">pathogen</a> pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> In general, low-latitude areas are at most risk of having decreased crop yields.<sup id="cite_ref-schneider_climate_change_and_agriculture_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schneider_climate_change_and_agriculture-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2007, the effects of regional climate change on agriculture have been small.<sup id="cite_ref-rosenzweig_observed_impacts_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rosenzweig_observed_impacts-43">[43]</a></sup> Changes in crop <a href="/wiki/Phenology" title="Phenology">phenology</a> provide important evidence of the response to recent regional climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Phenology is the study of natural phenomena that recur periodically, and how these phenomena relate to climate and seasonal changes.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> A significant advance in phenology has been observed for agriculture and forestry in large parts of the Northern Hemisphere.<sup id="cite_ref-rosenzweig_observed_impacts_43-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rosenzweig_observed_impacts-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Projections">Projections</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png" class="image"><img alt="Refer to caption" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png/350px-Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png" width="350" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png/525px-Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png/700px-Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png 2x" data-file-width="1322" data-file-height="694" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Projected_changes_in_crop_yields_at_different_latitudes_with_global_warming.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Projected changes in crop yields at different latitudes with global warming. This graph is based on several studies.<sup id="cite_ref-us_nrc_2011_fig_5.1_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us_nrc_2011_fig_5.1-110">[110]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png" class="image"><img alt="Refer to caption" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png/350px-Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png" width="350" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png/525px-Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png/700px-Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png 2x" data-file-width="1345" data-file-height="689" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Projected_changes_in_yields_of_selected_crops_with_global_warming.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Projected changes in yields of selected crops with global warming. This graph is based on several studies.<sup id="cite_ref-us_nrc_2011_fig_5.1_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us_nrc_2011_fig_5.1-110">[110]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
